## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (constitutive stress–strain–temperature modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables correspond to a constitutive relation where stress sigma depends on strain epsilon and temperature T via temperature-dependent elastic modulus, thermal strain offsets, and nonlinear (plastic/hyperelastic) hardening or softening behaviors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies with temperature)
- Polynomial modulus vs temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (empirical thermoelastic stiffness fit)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain subtraction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress from mechanical strain after thermal expansion)
- Thermoelastic with reference temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal strain relative to a reference temperature)
- Nonlinear (Landau-type) elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (odd-power nonlinearity for symmetric tension/compression response)
- Strain hardening power law: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic hardening / Hollomon-type dependence on strain)
- Temperature-softened hardening (separable form): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (thermal softening of flow stress)
- Coupled thermo-mechanical polynomial: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (first-order coupling of strain and temperature)
- Exponential stiffening (hyperelastic surrogate): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - c2) (rubber-like or large-strain stiffening behavior)
- Entropic (rubber) elasticity scaling: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (stress proportional to absolute temperature in entropic networks)
- Bilinear elastoplastic (piecewise via min/max): sigma = c0 * min(epsilon, c1) + (c2 + c3 * (epsilon - c1)) * max(epsilon - c1, 0) (elastic then post-yield tangent modulus)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; temperature enters primarily through a multiplicative modulus term (c0 + c1*T) or similar smooth function of T.
- Thermal expansion effects → sigma depends on a shifted strain (epsilon - c*T) or (epsilon - c*(T - T0)), reflecting stress-free thermal strain subtraction.
- Thermal softening of strength/stiffness → multiplicative factors that decrease with T such as exp(-c*T) or (c0 + c1*T)**c2 with negative effective slope over the operating range.
- Strain hardening (plasticity) → convex increasing sigma(epsilon) often captured by epsilon**c, epsilon + epsilon**c, or additive offset plus power law.
- Large-strain stiffening in polymers/hyperelasticity → rapidly increasing sigma with epsilon modeled by exp(c*epsilon) or combinations like (exp(c*epsilon) - 1).
- Tension–compression symmetry (when present) → odd-power expansions in epsilon (e.g., epsilon + epsilon**3) rather than even powers that break sign symmetry.
- Thermo-mechanical coupling beyond separability → cross terms like epsilon*T or epsilon**a * T**b indicate that temperature changes both slope and curvature of sigma vs epsilon.
- Yield-like transitions → piecewise-linear or hinge-type structures using min/max (or equivalent) to represent elastic-to-plastic switching at a characteristic strain.
